Youth Garden

Fragments of Spring 233

— Light Flight

Spring is here again, "Spring does not feel like spring to the poor family." It seems that those who are spiritually poor (Poors in Spirit) still don't feel like they have been described.

The tender yellow willows, the delicate warbling birds, the lively elementary school students, the vigorous runners, and the couples walking side by side whispering - on Jiangwan Road, in the eyes of ordinary people, in the eyes of Guangmei, are naturally enviable. In my eyes, however, it only gives me a fragment of profound emotion and silence.

I didn't feel as uncomfortable as Guangmei about the "clothes hanger of a Western dress." Sometimes I feel annoyed by the lack of freedom (I say honestly), and sometimes I get some pleasure in my subconscious. Naturally, they have no place in my conscious mind. However, I, who have always been arrogant and self-confident, have recently felt that I am just a girl. How unreliable people's morals are! Sometimes I even assume that they are pitiful bugs, and I even think of Feng Xiaoqing's poem "I wish I could get a drop of Yangzhi water and sprinkle it on the earth as a pair of lotus flowers." I smiled and secretly told Bing, and she also smiled and said, "If I had two bodies, one to let her fall and taste the taste of falling, is it better to fall willfully or to be well-behaved?"

Zhen in the next room often recites, "As flies to wanton boys are we to Gods, they kill us with their sports" (Like flies in the hands of children, we are played to death in the hands of Gods and demons). "Is that so?" I often ask myself after reciting it like her. "Is that really so?" However, Zhen is famous as "Westernized Daiyu" because of this. It's just that "Mr. Baoyu" has never met. Once I teased her (under the moonlight on Jiangwan Road after dinner) and said, "If Mr. Baoyu finds her, our Daiyu may have to be even more Westernized and become Clara Bow." She smiled and said, "Clara Bow is the best. If only I could transform myself into her."

Research on Suicide 234

— Han Ze

Suicide is not just an important research topic in psychiatry, but also a social problem that we cannot ignore, like crime, prostitution, poverty, unemployment, and marriage. Suicide is not a recent product of the civilized world; it has existed since ancient times. Before Christianity spread in Europe, suicide was morally accepted. In the Orient, especially in China and Japan, it was even more so. For example, loyal ministers to their rulers, and virtuous women to their husbands, often gained fame and were respected by the world for committing suicide. In Japan, before the Meiji Restoration, warriors who had committed wrong would disembowel themselves (the Japanese call it "Seppuku"), to apologize to their lords. However, this kind of suicide is a product of their special traditions and environment, and cannot be equated with the suicide we are discussing here. If you read Mr. Kuai An's "A Virtuous and Loyal Girl," you will understand that the so-called loyal ministers and virtuous women of ancient times who committed suicide to preserve their virtue were not only forced to do so by the social customs, systems, and morality of the time, but were also compelled by their elders to sacrifice themselves! Strictly speaking, this cannot be called "suicide," but rather "homicide."

Nowadays, suicide is increasing day by day. In civilized countries, this phenomenon is even more pronounced. Not only the number of suicides, but also the percentage of suicides per population, is increasing year by year, and this increase is very rapid, which is alarming. For example, in Germany, between 1836 and 1911, over a period of about 75 years, the national population increased by only 41%, while the number of suicides in Prussia increased from 1,446 to 8,179 (about 5.06 times), and in Saxony from 162 to 1,573 (about 9.7 times). Other countries have also experienced this phenomenon. For instance, between 1870 and 1900, a period of only 30 years, the number of suicides in Austria increased from 1,560 to 4,215 (about 2.7 times), in Italy from 836 to 2,040 (about 2.4 times), in France from 4,490 to 8,926 (about 2 times), in the United States from 1,495 to 2,896 (about 1.9 times), and in Switzerland from 321 to 746 (about 2.3 times). We are not sure if these statistics are reliable, but there is no doubt that suicide is becoming more common day by day. The number of suicides in Japan is even higher than in European and American countries. In 1916 (Year 5 of the Republic), there were 9,599 suicides, and by 1925 (Year 14 of the Republic), the number had increased to 12,249. Our country does not have precise statistics on the number of suicides, but according to the statistics of the Shanghai Special Municipal Government's Social Bureau, in July of the 18th year of the Republic, in Shanghai alone, there were as many as 265 suicide cases, of which 58 people died, 195 were rescued, and 3 were unclear. This is an increase of 28 cases compared to August of the 17th year of the Republic (237 cases). The number of suicides in Shanghai is increasing day by day, which is undeniable.

Why is it that the more developed the culture, the more suicides there are, and why do urban residents account for a larger proportion? On the one hand, the more advanced the society, the more complex the social organization and social life, and thus the more natural it is that desires cannot be fulfilled. On the other hand, material civilization gradually leads urban residents to become neurasthenic. The most common cause of suicide is the inability to fulfill some desire (such as unrequited love, world-weariness, etc.) or the loss of social status or property. Therefore, those with underdeveloped desires, and those who have no status or property to lose, such as the extremely poor, commit suicide less often. In addition to these external reasons, suicide is also caused by internal factors, such as mental excitement or abnormalities.

The age of suicide, regardless of gender, is most common between fifteen or sixteen and thirty years old, and men are more likely to commit suicide than women. According to Japanese statistics from 1928 (Year 17 of the Republic), the age of suicide among men is highest between 20 and 24 years old, with a total of 1,106 people, followed by 15 to 19 years old, with 596 people, and then 25 to 29 years old, with 702 people. Among women, the age of suicide is highest between 20 and 24 years old, with 792 people, followed by 15 to 19 years old, with 696 people. The reason why women commit suicide less often than men is because women have less direct responsibility for life and are less affected by the pain of bankruptcy and unemployment. The reasons for women's suicide are mostly related to sexual relations. Thus, regardless of gender, suicide is most common during adolescence. However, there are also many suicides among elderly people over sixty to eighty years old. They mostly commit suicide because of difficult living conditions, illness, loneliness, or family discord in their old age.

Another point that deserves our attention and interest is that in foreign countries, men commit suicide more often than women, but this is not the case in our country. Sometimes, women commit suicide much more often than men. According to the statistics of the Shanghai Special Municipal Social Bureau, in July of the 18th year of the Republic, among the 237 suicide cases in Shanghai, there were 116 men and 140 women, accounting for 54.69% of the total. Moreover, the number of suicides is highest in July and August. Regarding this, the Social Bureau attributes the reason to this: "If suicide is due to livelihood difficulties, then it should be most common during the coldest months of winter." However, in fact, it is not the case. Suicide is more common during the hot months of July and August, because suicide is often caused by quarrels. In July and August, people cannot endure the heat in their pigeonhole-like houses and go to the alleys to cool off, which naturally increases the opportunity to contact neighbors and increases the chance of neighborly quarrels, directly increasing the chance of suicide. Moreover, the depression of summer is enough to make women with weak will power unable to withstand the stimulation and turn to suicide. Among these 265 suicide cases, 147 were due to family problems, accounting for 57.43% of the total, which shows the drawbacks of our country's family system.

As for the method of suicide, it is also of great research value, because the method of suicide contains a kind of popularity. For example, in Japan, since 1902, after the high-achieving student Fujimura Misao of the First High School jumped into the Kegon Falls, there was a temporary surge in suicides by jumping into waterfalls, which became a kind of fashion. The authorities were caught off guard. Later, a poisonous drug called "Potassium bichromate" became popular. In 1917 and 1918 (Years 6 and 7 of the Republic), after a rat poison called "Nuko irazu" (No Need for Cats) was invented, eight or nine out of ten people who committed suicide used this rat poison to kill themselves. Recently, a new trick has emerged, and the suicide method of taking sleeping pills has become popular. For example, the famous writer Ryunosuke Akutagawa committed suicide by taking sleeping pills. In addition, there has always been a suicide method of using the railroad as a pillow (the Japanese call it "railway suicide"), but because the death is too tragic, it cannot become very popular. Thus, the suicide is dominated by this kind of fashion, which is not

Page 30

their intention. It can be said that it illustrates the extreme suggestibility and imitative nature of human beings. As for the suicide methods in China, the most common is taking poison, and most of them take opium. If we pay attention to the local news, we can understand this. According to the statistics of the Social Bureau, in the 265 suicide cases in July of the 18th year, 215 were by poisoning, accounting for 83.98% of the total, 10 by hanging, 21 by drowning, 2 by stabbing themselves, and 8 by swallowing gold.

If we talk about the psychology of suicide, we are not psychology experts, so we not only dare not say anything, but also have nothing to say. However, we can copy some excerpts from the suicide writer Ryunosuke Akutagawa's last letter, "Letter to an Old Friend," for reference (according to Shen Duanxian's translation):

"No one has ever realistically described the psychology of a suicide. This is probably because of the suicide's self-esteem or the suicide's lack of interest in his own psychology. I want to express this psychology very clearly in this last letter to you, although I may not tell you the motives for suicide. Renier, in his short story, described a suicide, but the protagonist in this short story does not know why he committed suicide. You can find many motives for suicide in the third page of the newspaper, such as financial difficulties, pain, or mental anguish, but according to my experience, these are not all of the motives, but only the process of expressing these motives. Most people who commit suicide, like the one described by Renier, do not know why they are committing suicide. This is the same as our behavior in general, which contains complex motives, but my suicide is at most a vague unease, an unspeakable and vague unease. You may not believe my words, but my years of experience have taught me that people who are close to me, as long as they are not in a similar situation to me, listen to my words like songs in the wind. Therefore, I do not want to blame you either. In the past two years, I have been thinking about death. In a calm mood, I have been reading Maerlinte. During this period, Maerlinte cleverly described the morality of dying with abstract words, but I want to describe the same thing more concretely. Compassion for my family is not enough to be considered before this desire. This probably sounds inhumane to you, but if it is inhumane, then one side of me is indeed inhumane. I have a duty to describe everything realistically. The first thing I think about is how to die without pain. Hanging is certainly a means that is consistent with this purpose, but when I imagine my appearance after I hang myself, I cannot help but feel a kind of 'aesthetic aversion': Drowning is not a solution for those of us who can swim. Even if it succeeds, the pain must be greater than hanging. Stabbing and I will feel an aesthetic aversion. Using a gun or a knife, because of the trembling of my hands, there is a possibility of failure. Jumping from a high building is certainly not good-looking. For these reasons, I decided to use medicine. Suicide by medicine is probably more painful than hanging, but this method, in addition to not having an aesthetic aversion, also has the advantage of not having the danger of resuscitation. However, it is certainly not easy for me to buy this kind of medicine. After I decided to commit suicide in my heart, I took advantage of every opportunity to look for this kind of medicine, and at the same time, I wanted to seek a little knowledge of toxicology. The second thing I thought about was the problem of the place of death. My family must rely on my inheritance after my death. My inheritance is only one hundred ping of land, my house, my copyright, and two thousand yuan in savings. I am worried that in the future, no one will want to buy my house because of my suicide, and I feel envy for the rich people who have villas. You must find this funny, and I myself find this funny, but in fact, when I think of this, I feel deeply inconvenienced, and on the one hand, I cannot avoid this inconvenience. I only want to not let people other than my family see my body after I commit suicide. I do not regard suicide as a sin like the red-haired people. The Buddha even affirmed his disciple's suicide in the Agama Sutra, and the sycophants explain this affirmation as only applicable to times of desperation, but in the eyes of third parties, 'times of desperation' are not tragic and hopeless times when death is the only option. People who commit suicide always commit suicide in 'times of desperation.' It can be said that it takes courage to commit suicide before times of desperation, because we humans are human beasts, afraid of death like animals. The so-called vitality is really another name for animal power. I am a human beast, but judging from the fact that I am already tired of eating and sex, my animal power has probably gradually disappeared. I am now living in a world of ice-cold and clear nerves. If we can be content with eternal sleep, then even if it cannot be regarded as happiness for ourselves, it can also be regarded as peace." We will not talk about the suicide of a writer like Akutagawa for the time being, and in fact, we are not qualified to speak. However, I have some opinions on general suicide. "Suicide is cowardly." This is certainly true in a certain sense. Some people think that they should commit suicide if everything in the world cannot go as they wish. This is too cowardly. There are also some ignorant women who want to take their own lives because of some small quarrels or being scolded. That is really ridiculous and pitiful. Try asking yourself, "Are those worthless things like quarrels and scolding worth my life?" Then you will understand. To commit suicide because of a quarrel or being scolded may be the highest means of coercion against the other party, but if you die, where is your coercion then? If you are heartbroken, I think you can use this heartbreak as a stimulant to boost your courage. If your career fails, I think you can use this failure as experience and as a weapon for advancement. Don't you remember that "failure is the mother of success"? If you commit suicide because of family problems, then your descendants will probably commit suicide because of family problems for generations. If you feel that your family is not good and that China's family system is very bad, then you should pluck up your courage to reform your own family and start a revolution in China's family system. If you must take the path of suicide, then please think again, is this kind of thing worth my life? Is my life only worth this much? When you really get to the city of unjust deaths or are about to step into the city of unjust deaths, don't you know what regrets will arise? I advise those who want to take the path of suicide to pluck up their courage and try again. If you still feel that you must die, then die.
